FIELD REPORT NO.
This is UNEVALUATED PROFESSIONALION. SOURCE GRADINGS ARE DEFINITIVE. APPROVAL OF CONTENT IS TENTATIVE.
SOURCE: A former Cuban IS officer who served with the Cuban Intelligence Service
until April 1694.
Headquarters Comments
The following report is one of a series containing personality information
provided by the source and includes supplemental information from the
records of this Agency.
It is requested that the addressees take no action on any of the individuals
mentioned in the personality reports without first checking with this Agency.
Esther GAVILAN Rosales is the wife of Rogelio RODRIGUEZ
Lopez, the Subject of the above referenced report. 1
Headquarters Comment
1. Official travel manifests reveal that Esther GAVILAN Rosales arrived
in Mexico City from Cuba on 15 December 1961 and carried a diplomatic
passport; departed Mexico City for Cuba on 27 April 1962, carrying
Cuban diplomatic passport number D/61-538; and arrived in Mexico
from Habana on 8 July 1963, carrying Cuban diplomatic passport
number D/63/455.

SUBJECT Shipment of Explosives to
DATE DIST. 25 August 1964

PLACE & Washington, D. C.
DATE ACGAugust 1964
FRED REPORT NO.
THIS IS UNEVALUATED INFORMATION SOURCE CLADINGS ARE DEFINITIVE. APFERIAL OF CONTENT IS TENTATIVE.
SOURCE: A former Cuban IS officer who served with the Cuban Intelligence
Service until April 1964.
Following is a translation of a report which source
wrote concerning a shipment of explosives to Mexico:
"The Communist Party of El Salvador had asked me to
send them twenty-five, one quarter pound packages of
gelatin explosives. They requested that the explosives be
sent to Mexico where they would recover them and take
them to El Salvador.
"In view of the request, I spoke with Manuel PINEIRO
regarding the shipment itself, as well as the amount.
PINEIRO answered by telling me to do so.
"During my trip to Mexico (March 1964) I spoke with
Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez regarding this shipment and he told
me that there was no need of my sending the explosives
to Mexico as this type of explosive, was available in the
Embassy. I then told RODRIGUEZ that I would answer the
request from El Salvador.
"Upon returning to Cuba I spoke with PINEIRO, who told
me not to send the explosives as the orders now were to
send nothing but money due to the recent exposure of the
arms shipment to Venezuela."

CONCIDENTIAL
Date:
August 20, 1964
To:
Mr. Winston M. Scott
From: 11 Clark D. Anderson
Legal Attache
Re:
ROGELIO RODRIGUEZ LOPEZ
This document is for the use of your
agency. and neither it nor its
contents chould be further distributed
without appropriate authorization.
Reference is made to your communication of
May 26, 1964, that the subject and his chauffeur planned
to travel to Nuevo Laredo to pick up a new automobile.
A confidential source, who has furnished
reliable information in the past, furnished the follow-
ing information on July 24, 1964:
ROGELIO RODRIGUEZ, of 160 Uurgas Street,
Mexico City, was in Nuevo Laredo on May 27, 1964, to
obtain an automobile for the Cuban Embassy in Mexico
City. A 1964 black Ford Galaxy 500, Serial Number
4B62X150451, was delivered to RODRIGUEZ on May 27, 1964.
RODRIGUEZ appeared to be about 23 years of age,
and it is known that he was buying cigarettes and radios
during his stay in Nuevo Laredo.
CONFIDENTIAL
Group 1
Excluded from Automatic
Downgrading and Declarsification


The Mexican diplomatic license plates #333 were
placed on the above mentioned vehicle.

Rapublica de Cuba
Ministerio de Relaciones Calesteres
Pensapete Sjolomásica
9/30/20


14/02/2000
3
0
Ei
de Velarinnes Exteriores,
combre
Jasapurte Diplomáttra a fano de
St. Poyelio Rodriguez ofpecs
para que por la vita que más le contenga se dirija a
Eccidos Clindos Pexroanos
boure ejercerá las funidones de Jecenlano oüberspto
y la Ginsyoda de Casa
fur tanto: en nombre del Sr. Dresidente de la Hepublica,
cortana a las Autoribidas de la Cación le facilitar su embarca u
la ganen las considarias delibida a su rango. y ruesga
y requiterre a las de los países extranjeros por Bunde transi-
tare, que le prezent tobó al favor u aguola que merezir u le re-
concorran las unumitabres y perrogulíhues que confucue al Derechlo
he geotes corresponden a los be su chase; laisi asegu-
caraia la recipercibad en Cuba en caso anilagos.
Joho de 1963
Réginlom
de Riziatones
de Lago
Laz

3. A fairly reliable source in a document dated 4 March 1964
said that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, at the 18 January 1964 Cuban
Embassy staff reeting, was given the assignment as Political

4. In a report dated 26 April 1964 it was reported that Rogelio

his contacts in Mexico.
5. On 28 April 1964 it was reported that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, a
known Cuban intelligence service officer, left Mexico for
Cuba on 25. April 1964 for a permanent change of station.
6. In the 17 May 1964 issue of Hoy it was reported that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy in
Mexico City, left Cuba on 16 May 1964 to return to duty in
Mexico.
7. A fairly reliable source in a report dated 5 June 1964 stated
that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy
in Mexico City, is the son of a Communist Party member and
that he (RODRIGUEZ) previously worked in the Foreign Office
on Mexican matters in the Latin American Political
Department. Source also said that he thought RODRIGUEZ
probably worked for Manucl PINEIRO.

SOURCE A former Cuban IS Officer who served with the Cuban
Intelligence Service until April 1964.
Headquarters Comment. The following report is one of a
series containing personality information provided by the
source and includes supplemental information from the
records of this Agency.
1. Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez, who uses the pseudonyms "Kedardo,"
"Casimiro," and "Jose Antonio," is an officer of the
Direccion General de Inteligencia (DGI - General Directorate
of Intelligence) stationed in Mexico City, Mexico.
2. RODRIGUEZ, who was born in approximately 1940, is five
feet eight inches tall, has a husky build, a reddish
complexion and blond hair. 1,2,3,4,5,6,7
Headquarters Comments.
1. A usually reliable source in a report dated 29 March
1962 stated that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ Lopez is the
number of any of the Cuban Embassy in Mexico City.
Source also. said that RODRIGUEZ had plans to see
Major Alfonso PRERA, leader of the 13 November Group
in Mexico on 24 March 1962.
2. In a report dated 14 February 1964 Rogelio RODRIGUEZ
Lopez was reported to be the second secretary of the
Cuban Embassy in Mexico City.

Mar 22 3 55 PM 65
3. A fairly reliable source in a document dated 4 March 1964
said that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, at the 18 January 1964 Cuban
Embassy staff meeting, was given the assignment as Political
Reporting Officer.
4. In a report dated 26 April 1964 it was reported that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy in
Mexico. City, uses the pseudonyms "Chele" and "Gorrin" with
his contacts in Mexico.
5. On 28 April 1964 it was reported that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, a
known. Cuban. intelligence service officer, left Mexico for
Cuba on 25 April 1964 for a permanent change of station.
6. In the 17 May 1964 issue of Hoy it was reported that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy in
Mexico City, left Cuba on 16 May 1964 to return to duty in
Mexico.
7. A fairly reliable source in a report dated 5 June 1964 stated
that Rogelio RODRIGUEZ, second secretary of the Cuban Embassy
in Mexico City, is the son of a Communist Party member. and
that he (RODRIGUEZ) previously worked in the Foreign Office
of the American American Political
Department. See in the National American Political
Responsibility. See also a Finance he thought RODRIGUEZ
probably worked for Manet PINERIO.

NO FOREIGN DISSEM


FROM : Amembassy MEXICO
SUBJECT: Changes in Soviet Bloc Diplomatic Personnel in Mexico
The Mexico City daily Excelsior reported on June 17 that Regelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopez, Second Secretary of the Cuban Embassy, was given a
farewell party by his friends. Rodriguez recently made a trip to
Cuba and, at that time, it was rumored that he would be transferred.
Instead, he returned to Mexico. The Embassy possesses no other
information regarding Rodriguez possible re-assignment.
For the Charge d'Affaires ad interim:
Wallace W. Stuart
Counselor of Embassy
for Political Affairs
EXCERPT
EXCERPT
DST-11954
27 June 1964
DST-11954
27 June 1964


FROH : Amembassy MEXICO
SUBJECT: Changes in Soviet Bloc Diplomatic Personnel in Mexico
The Mexico City daily Ercelisor reported on June 17 that Rogelio
RODRIGUEZ Lopes, Second Secretary of the Cuban Embassy, was given a
farewell party by his friends. Rodrigues recently made a trip to
Cuba and, at that time, it was rumored that he would be transferred.
Instead, he returned to Mexico. The Embassy possesses no other
information regarding Rodrigues' possible re-assignment.
For the Charge d'Affaires ad interim:
Wallace W. Stuart
Counselor of Embassy
for Political Affairs

Meeting: 24. September 1964, AMINT-1 and AMSESS-1; and 25 September
1964, Lavrence F. BARKER (C/O), AMIT-1 and AMSESS-1. AMSESS-1
returned to Cuba and did not make subsequent meetings with KUBARK,
14. On the subject of "I." (Direccion General de Inteligencia),
the following exchange took place:
C/O: Who is the "M" chief in the Embassy I in Mexico J?
A-1: Vega. (Manuel VESA Pores)
C/O: Who else is with "M"?
A-1: Rogelio (Rzgello RCRIGUEZ Lopes). But he is just
a second rater.

1 January 1964
MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD
FROM
:
Lavrence F. Barker
SUBJECT :
Meeting with LITAMIL-9, 6 January 1964
1. A meeting was held with L-9 from 2000 hours until 2320 hours 6
Jan -- pick-up and drop-off were made by car, the meeting took place at
B's home with B's wife, working the gate.
2. L-9 was unusually depressed -- had just received a letter from
Spain indicating that his sister had been forced to leave her work as a
result of excessive fatigue and the "never ending round of discussions
and study circles" etc. She had not received much sympathy from the
Cuban FOUNIN and her request for 2 months leave in Spain was denied pending
the decision to be made to a quite fond of his sister, took this news to
heart and it ate away at the time and compounded his usual miserable feeling,
the first part of the meeting was taken up in a C/O delivered pept talk.
3. L-9 had the following to reports:
a. At the evening reception at 2 Jan at the Embassy, the TASS
representative remarked that he believed KIRNCHIEBY did not
be the most important and adversary celebrations because
of the revelation of an exile plot to bomb Havana -- revelations
which came about as the result of the arrest by the US Coast
Guard of some war-like Cubans with bombs in their possession.
The TASS man said that he believed that MIRSHIEBY would show
up someday in Harana quite unumounced as add CASTRO in the USSR.
The Teresa FROENZA may be hired back by the Embassy - APARICIO
recently remarked to L-9, "Surely they will re-hire her." It
is quite clear that APARICIO doesn't want her in his office again
to be the most important and heavily if she were to be retired one
would work in the main behalf of the House.
In regard to the PROENZA firing, ROJAS of Cubana de Avicacion,
who is married to Teresa's sister, said that he had written to
FOHIN Raul ROA in her behalf but had received no reply.
d. Ambassador HERMANDEZ Armas sent a Christmas present to OROSSTZA
of the Mexican Foreign Office this year -- it was really a New
Year's present, sent 31 Dec. L-9 does not know what it was.
4. L-9 was asked what all the nucleus was at the airport on 5 Jan. This
drew a blank. B then said he had heard that a pleaum of Embassy officers was
out there apparently guarding someone who was on his way to Cuba. L-9 didn't
know anything about it. B remarked that two Cuban officials were supposedly
on the flight to Havana - one from the Embassy in Montierideo. At this point,
the message was the most important, but it was a very good thing to be
related the details of a conversation he had had with Earl&EREZ Friman at the
Embassy on 2 Jan - details sent to HQS separately by cable. (See MEXI T6-99
)
L-9 was not aware that PEREZ had been on the 5 Jan flight -- he described his
perfectly. He was not made aware of KUBARN involvement in the alleged "assaults"
nor was he told anything about PREZ? appearance at PEEJIDE.
5. L-9 identified a number of persons appearing in the photos taken at
the diplomatic reception held at the Embassy 2 Jan. Identifications were noted

27 April 1964
Neetin. with LITAMIL-3 to 'Debrisf hia meeting with L-7
Next Meetinr: 30 April
1. Attached 1r self-explanatory report from LITAMIL-7. Pull
of little goodies, all of operational nature.
Floyd N. AIMONET
1.- Mannel Vega agri acreditado como Fercera
Secretario y viene a sustituir temperal
mente al Tercer Secretario Rogalio Ro-
driguez. Sus funciones en la Embagada:
p.9921
Proparar-valijas, Recibiratirdas y
personajes cubanco. No se sabe que tiem-
po durarávkus funciones en México.
N
2.- Rogelio Rodríguez, Tercer Secretario, salidaz
para la Habana y según dice permanecerá en
p.7365 dicho luza/mas o menos unas cuatro sema-
nasa.
3.- El correo Almara,que regresó del Canadá,
dice que el Embajador Amoriao Cruz, se en-
cuentra en Cuba.
4.- Grilio Samá, Consul en Veracruz, se encun-
tra aquil en Mexico. No le da importancia
8.8694
A1 suceso de Veracruz. Eotá muy seguro que
nada le gucedera. R= ereo que mañana juvées
regresars e Veracruz.
5.- El nombraniento de Grotlaza, causó muy bue-
na impresion en la Demida.
6.- Teresa Proenza, tiene ordenes de visitar lo ne-
nos que pueda a la Embajada. No ne sabe
p.3696
cundo salidrá hacia Cuba.
7.- Berta Pino, tiene a su cuidado el Registro
de las Visas.
8.- En el Hall de la Embalada, casi diarinmente
se runco todo el percani de la Embajada pa-
ra dicutir el asunto del Brasil y lo de la
Base de Guantanaro.
9.- El mesero Peroira, insiste en hablar con el
amigo.
10.- Han anviado a los Demabladas amigos y no ami-
gas copias de "Minotorgravo" de las declara-
ciones de Fidel sobre el problema del Brasil.

mesas. -Inzunza! que al or.Arazil

Salida al 222401.- 1616hs. - Rogelio Rodríguez con García
Romero le pregunta que a que horas se va el avión. Romero: -
que mas o menos como a las cinco.- Rogelio: que hace falta
mandar-una cosa urgente para la Tabana hoy. Romero: que cuan
to se van a tardar porque el avión casi ya está listo, que hay
1365
muy poco pasaje.- Rogelio que llamó a Cubana y que le dijeron

rá tiempo- Romero: que si llegan antes de las cinco que el

1096.-
Entrada a las 1607.-hs.- HF Jorge Rojas con Rogelio le pro
gunta que auien lo llama dé la embajada. Rogelio que eran' ellos
1365
que el problema que hay que es que hay que mandar para la Haba
(8)
na una cosa urgente y que como el vuelo no llegue posiblemen
te hasta el domingo, que eso tiene que estar en la Habana an
tos del vierne.- Rojas: que el avión en este momento ya es
ta subiendo a bordo el pasaja ya.- Rogoljo: que es una cosa
super urgente y que si las cosas no están en cinco minutos.-
Rogelio: que en cinco minutos no pueden estar.- Rojas: que en
tonces se quedaron, que lo siente en el alma pro que ya está
todo mino a bordo.- Rogelio: que correcto.- Rojas: que para
el viernesa hay vuelo.- Rogelio: que si no se puede tratar de
Rojas: que no que allí está la autoridad que está furio
sa porque los tripulantes han demorado que deben de haber sali
do hace 45 minutos y que tiene la Comandancia encima.- Que -
mande las cosas pero sin asegurarle que lo van a esperar.--- -

: Meeting with LITANIL-9, 30 Jan 1964
2. L-9 reported on the following:
a. On Saturday 18 Jan at the usual Embassy staff reeting,
several new assignments were passed out.

Reporting Officer.

Cultural Department. Later on he spoke with Rogolio
RCRIOUZE and told L-9 aftomaras, "Nagelio doesn't seen
to trust me."

COMMON
4715 -- BELOW SYSTEM BETWEEN IDENS A AND B ) ; THAT HE ("CHELE")

PHONE CONVERSATION) THAT "CHELE" IS ROGELIO. (PROBABLY ROGELIO

3. IDEN B NOW CALLS EMBASSY EACH DAY, USUALLY AT 1300 HRS,
AND ASKS FOR "GORRIN", ANOTHER NAME USED BY "CHELE".
4. IDEN A PLANS RETURN MEXICO CITY 3 MARCH AND HAS BEEN
INSTRUCTED BY ERYTHROID/3 TO REMAIN THERE UNTIL IDEN B LEAVES.
